B. Matcrial Processed

In October, the Scatton was provided by the LIENVOY LP with 13S

pages uf daily resumes from all lines, lo pages of resumce from the Cuban

Ines, 17 pages from the Czech lines and 12l pagus from the Soviet lies.

In addition the taped reels from the Soviet and Cauch Iines were turned over

for the transcription of the Russian and Cacch conversatlong. There were

also provided 11 pleces of other miscellancous matertal.

C. Lialson

Because of the urgency of business during the month of Ocuiet, the

COS met with LIERGO and LIELEGANT more frequently, LITENSOR ex-

pressed his gratefulness through LIELEGANT on provlling, him with repores:

on the political scene in the Far Eist countries that he had visited. On 25

Ocrober, LITENSOR was given the report on the Cuban aluation which was

sent to the Station In DIR 44302, LITENSOR was also shown pholos of the

Soviet missile bases in Cuba, After mecring with high-lovel Mexican efficials,

the Chief of Station reported in MEXI 2397 on their attitudes of the U.S..

quarantine of Cuba and the stopping of further progreds on Soviet missile

bases there.

D. Exploitation of Material

An example of Information obtained through LIENVOY was the

attempt of Vicente Lombardo Toledano, prominent leftlet Mexican politician,

to make an appolntment witli the Mexican Government In regard to Cuba,

Lombardo Tolcuano was prompted by General Lazaro Cardenas to trito

influence the President. (see MEXI 2404)

dally resumes, 40 pages of resumes from the Cuban lines and 35 other

C. Exploitation of Material

The following are examples of Information obtained through LIENVOY.

1. In a telephone conversation from San Luis Potosi, Col.

Renato Vega Amador, DFS Chiel, told Capt, de la Barrera of the

Mexico City DFS that "things are happening In San.Luis Potost",

and that "something bad would happen" in Monterrey and Mexico

City againsi the Federal Govemnient and that of the State of San

Luis Potost, (MEXI 1600)

2. Joe Nordmann, Secretary of the International Assoelation of

Democratic Lawyera (LADL), spoke with Angelica Arenal de Alfaro

Siguciros about hla plan to see do President of Mexico to have David

Allaro Siquelros released from prison. (MEXI 1676)

3. According lo employees of the Prensa Latina, employees had

not been paid for some time and the financial situation of the Agency

was "desperate". (MEXI 1670)

D. Llalson.

port on Cuauhtemoc Cardenas.

of Station was told that Cardenas would nor be a candidate for "Water

un Indonesia, Japan 'and India be made available for LITENSOR's use on

hls approaching visit to these countries in late September.

pouched io Mexico City. Chief of Station according to DIR 31814.

inent Mexican Communis:, and A, B. Magill, Nagill invited Aguilar to lunch

n addition, Christmas glits were presented to LIENVOY/2 b

he case officer (Edeland) and by Arnold F. Archart. Glits were also

given to the personnel working in the LP base.

E. Security

There were no significant security problems during the months

under consideration.

F. Techalcal

promptly and efiectively.

There were no technical problems that could not be dealt with

keep all equipment operating continuously and efficiently.

MENORANDUM FOR:

SUBJECT:

REFERENCE:

Chief, WH/3

CW Signals on Telephone Tap

HIMMA-14977, 19 May 1960

1. A technical analysis of referoncestap indicates that the

CW Morse signals probably were picked up incidental to the primary

tap and did not actually occur on Line #2. This is borne out both

from a technical standpoint (signal to noiso ratio, oxtraneous CW

signals, etc.) as well as from the contes? of the mossages them.

selves.

The latter, as will be noted in the altachod transcript,

primarily concern arrivals and departures of what appear to be

small maritime vossols. The two radio calls mentioned, 1. o.

"XBRB2" and "XBRP", are listed in tho International Call Sign

Book as follows:

XBRB - Vera Cruz (19-10N, 96-15W)

XBRP - Pichilingue (24-12N, 110-20 W)

The originating station in this case was Pichilingue.

2. Madassuristiere is some good reason why a port.

authority on the west coast of Mexico would be sending trailic of

this nature to an east coast port, However, jyff how those

..peiatily

particular signals happened in be picked up on

Sim Brooks lino

is open to conjecturo.

It is our guess shat it probably was due

to one of the following reasona:

• A radio transmitter may be situated near the

sap and is serving as a relay station between Pichilingu

and Vera Cruz, Il this is the case it may be giving off

strong radio frequency signals which possibly are being

SEGRET

= 2=

Do The equipment used in conjunction with the tap

may be serving as a poor radio receivar, using the telephone

Line as au antenna.

c. The CW signals pussibly are being picked up

inductively, i e. from anosher phone line which is in

closo proximity to Line $?.

his theory seems unlikel

owever, aince the transmission of CW signals from on

const to the other via telephone lines would be a slow and

impractical procedure.

dio rom th standpoint of technical interose, hardes

seuntiate any of the above conjectures.

furnish additional analysis an transcripts should similar signals

be noted in the future.
